This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n    25→    /// that is associated with the task.\n    26→    /// The value of this field gets passed to all functions that are part of\n    27→    /// the vtable as the first parameter.\n    28→    data: *const (),\n    29→    /// Virtual function pointer table that customizes the behavior of this waker.\n    30→    vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable,\n    31→}\n    32→\n    33→impl RawWaker {\n    34→    /// Creates a new `RawWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n    35→    ///\n    36→    /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n    37→    /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n    38→    /// that is associated with the task.\n    39→    /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n    40→    /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n    41→    ///\n    42→    /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n    43→    /// thread safe type such as an `Arc<T: Send + Sync>`\n    44→    /// when used to construct a [`Waker`]. This restriction is lifted when\n    45→    /// constructing a [`LocalWaker`], which allows using types that do not implement\n    46→    /// <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code> like `Rc<T>`.\n    47→    ///\n    48→    /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker` which gets created\n    49→    /// from a `RawWaker`. For each operation on the `Waker`, the associated\n    50→    /// function in the `vtable` of the underlying `RawWaker` will be called.\n    51→    #[inline]\n    52→    #[rustc_promotable]\n    53→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    54→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    55→    #[must_use]\n    56→    pub const fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> RawWaker {\n    57→        RawWaker { data, vtable }\n    58→    }\n    59→\n    60→    #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n    61→    const NOOP: RawWaker = {\n    62→        const VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = RawWakerVTable::new(\n    63→            // Cloning just returns a new no-op raw waker\n    64→            |_| RawWaker::NOOP,\n    65→            // `wake` does nothing\n    66→            |_| {},\n    67→            // `wake_by_ref` does nothing\n    68→            |_| {},\n    69→            // Dropping does nothing as we don't allocate anything\n    70→            |_| {},\n    71→        );\n    72→        RawWaker::new(ptr::null(), &VTABLE)\n    73→    };\n    74→}\n    75→\n    76→/// A virtual function pointer table (vtable) that specifies the behavior\n    77→/// of a [`RawWaker`].\n    78→///\n    79→/// The pointer passed to all functions inside the vtable is the `data` pointer\n    80→/// from the enclosing [`RawWaker`] object.\n    81→///\n    82→/// The functions inside this struct are only intended to be called on the `data`\n    83→/// pointer of a properly constructed [`RawWaker`] object from inside the\n    84→/// [`RawWaker`] implementation. Calling one of the contained functions using\n    85→/// any other `data` pointer will cause undefined behavior.\n    86→///\n    87→/// Note that while this type implements `PartialEq`, comparing function pointers, and hence\n    88→/// comparing structs like this that contain function pointers, is unreliable: pointers to the same\n    89→/// function can compare inequal (because functions are duplicated in multiple codegen units), and\n    90→/// pointers to *different* functions can compare equal (since identical functions can be\n    91→/// deduplicated within a codegen unit).\n    92→///\n    93→/// # Thread safety\n    94→/// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\n    95→/// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\n    96→/// <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\n    97→/// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\n    98→/// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\n    99→/// they must do so atomically.\n   100→///\n   101→/// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\n   102→/// these functions don't need to be thread safe. This means that <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>\n   103→///  data can be stored in the data pointer, and reference counting does not need any atomic\n   104→/// synchronization. This is because [`LocalWaker`] is not thread safe itself, so it cannot\n   105→/// be sent across threads.\n   106→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   107→#[allow(unpredictable_function_pointer_comparisons)]\n   108→#[derive(PartialEq, Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n   109→pub struct RawWakerVTable {\n   110→    /// This function will be called when the [`RawWaker`] gets cloned, e.g. when\n   111→    /// the [`Waker`] in which the [`RawWaker`] is stored gets cloned.\n   112→    ///\n   113→    /// The implementation of this function must retain all resources that are\n   114→    /// required for this additional instance of a [`RawWaker`] and associated\n   115→    /// task. Calling `wake` on the resulting [`RawWaker`] should result in a wakeup\n   116→    /// of the same task that would have been awoken by the original [`RawWaker`].\n   117→    clone: unsafe fn(*const ()) -> RawWaker,\n   118→\n   119→    /// This function will be called when `wake` is called on the [`Waker`].\n   120→    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n   121→    ///\n   122→    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n   123→    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n   124→    /// associated task.\n   125→    wake: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n   126→\n   127→    /// This function will be called when `wake_by_ref` is called on the [`Waker`].\n   128→    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n   129→    ///\n   130→    /// This function is similar to `wake`, but must not consume the provided data\n   131→    /// pointer.\n   132→    wake_by_ref: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n   133→\n   134→    /// This function will be called when a [`Waker`] gets dropped.\n   135→    ///\n   136→    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n   137→    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n   138→    /// associated task.\n   139→    drop: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n   140→}\n   141→\n   142→impl RawWakerVTable {\n   143→    /// Creates a new `RawWakerVTable` from the provided `clone`, `wake`,\n   144→    /// `wake_by_ref`, and `drop` functions.\n   145→    ///\n   146→    /// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\n   147→    /// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\n   148→    /// <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\n   149→    /// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\n   150→    /// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\n   151→    /// they must do so atomically.\n   152→    ///\n   153→    /// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\n   154→    /// these functions don't need to be thread safe. This means that <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>\n   155→    /// data can be stored in the data pointer, and reference counting does not need any atomic\n   156→    /// synchronization. This is because [`LocalWaker`] is not thread safe itself, so it cannot\n   157→    /// be sent across threads.\n   158→    /// # `clone`\n   159→    ///\n   160→    /// This function will be called when the [`RawWaker`] gets cloned, e.g. when\n   161→    /// the [`Waker`]/[`LocalWaker`] in which the [`RawWaker`] is stored gets cloned.\n   162→    ///\n   163→    /// The implementation of this function must retain all resources that are\n   164→    /// required for this additional instance of a [`RawWaker`] and associated\n   165→    /// task. Calling `wake` on the resulting [`RawWaker`] should result in a wakeup\n   166→    /// of the same task that would have been awoken by the original [`RawWaker`].\n   167→    ///\n   168→    /// # `wake`\n   169→    ///\n   170→    /// This function will be called when `wake` is called on the [`Waker`].\n   171→    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n   172→    ///\n   173→    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n   174→    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n   175→    /// associated task.\n   176→    ///\n   177→    /// # `wake_by_ref`\n   178→    ///\n   179→    /// This function will be called when `wake_by_ref` is called on the [`Waker`].\n   180→    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n   181→    ///\n   182→    /// This function is similar to `wake`, but must not consume the provided data\n   183→    /// pointer.\n   184→    ///\n   185→    /// # `drop`\n   186→    ///\n   187→    /// This function will be called when a [`Waker`]/[`LocalWaker`] gets\n   188→    /// dropped.\n   189→    ///\n   190→    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n   191→    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n   192→    /// associated task.\n   193→    #[rustc_promotable]\n   194→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   195→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   196→    pub const fn new(\n   197→        clone: unsafe fn(*const ()) -> RawWaker,\n   198→        wake: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n   199→        wake_by_ref: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n   200→        drop: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n   201→    ) -> Self {\n   202→        Self { clone, wake, wake_by_ref, drop }\n   203→    }\n   204→}\n   205→\n   206→#[derive(Debug)]\n   207→enum ExtData<'a> {\n   208→    Some(&'a mut dyn Any),\n   209→    None(()),\n   210→}\n   211→\n   212→/// The context of an asynchronous task.\n   213→///\n   214→/// Currently, `Context` only serves to provide access to a [`&Waker`](Waker)\n   215→/// which can be used to wake the current task.\n   216→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   217→#[lang = \"Context\"]\n   218→pub struct Context<'a> {\n   219→    waker: &'a Waker,\n   220→    local_waker: &'a LocalWaker,\n   221→    ext: AssertUnwindSafe<ExtData<'a>>,\n   222→    // Ensure we future-proof against variance changes by forcing\n   223→    // the lifetime to be invariant (argument-position lifetimes\n   224→    // are contravariant while return-position lifetimes are\n   225→    // covariant).\n   226→    _marker: PhantomData<fn(&'a ()) -> &'a ()>,\n   227→    // Ensure `Context` is `!Send` and `!Sync` in order to allow\n   228→    // for future `!Send` and / or `!Sync` fields.\n   229→    _marker2: PhantomData<*mut ()>,\n   230→}\n   231→\n   232→impl<'a> Context<'a> {\n   233→    /// Creates a new `Context` from a [`&Waker`](Waker).\n   234→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   235→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n   236→    #[must_use]\n   237→    #[inline]\n   238→    pub const fn from_waker(waker: &'a Waker) -> Self {\n   239→        ContextBuilder::from_waker(waker).build()\n   240→    }\n   241→\n   242→    /// Returns a reference to the [`Waker`] for the current task.\n   243→    #[inline]\n   244→    #[must_use]\n   245→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   246→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n   247→    pub const fn waker(&self) -> &'a Waker {\n   248→        &self.waker\n   249→    }\n   250→\n   251→    /// Returns a reference to the [`LocalWaker`] for the current task.\n   252→    #[inline]\n   253→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   254→    pub const fn local_waker(&self) -> &'a LocalWaker {\n   255→        &self.local_waker\n   256→    }\n   257→\n   258→    /// Returns a reference to the extension data for the current task.\n   259→    #[inline]\n   260→    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n   261→    pub const fn ext(&mut self) -> &mut dyn Any {\n   262→        // FIXME: this field makes Context extra-weird about unwind safety\n   263→        // can we justify AssertUnwindSafe if we stabilize this? do we care?\n   264→        match &mut self.ext.0 {\n   265→            ExtData::Some(data) => *data,\n   266→            ExtData::None(unit) => unit,\n   267→        }\n   268→    }\n   269→}\n   270→\n   271→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   272→impl fmt::Debug for Context<'_> {\n   273→    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n   274→        f.debug_struct(\"Context\").field(\"waker\", &self.waker).finish()\n   275→    }\n   276→}\n   277→\n   278→/// A Builder used to construct a `Context` instance\n   279→/// with support for `LocalWaker`.\n   280→///\n   281→/// # Examples\n   282→/// ```\n   283→/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n   284→/// use std::task::{ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker, Poll};\n   285→/// use std::future::Future;\n   286→///\n   287→/// let local_waker = LocalWaker::noop();\n   288→/// let waker = Waker::noop();\n   289→///\n   290→/// let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(&waker)\n   291→///     .local_waker(&local_waker)\n   292→///     .build();\n   293→///\n   294→/// let mut future = std::pin::pin!(async { 20 });\n   295→/// let poll = future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx);\n   296→/// assert_eq!(poll, Poll::Ready(20));\n   297→///\n   298→/// ```\n   299→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   300→#[derive(Debug)]\n   301→pub struct ContextBuilder<'a> {\n   302→    waker: &'a Waker,\n   303→    local_waker: &'a LocalWaker,\n   304→    ext: ExtData<'a>,\n   305→    // Ensure we future-proof against variance changes by forcing\n   306→    // the lifetime to be invariant (argument-position lifetimes\n   307→    // are contravariant while return-position lifetimes are\n   308→    // covariant).\n   309→    _marker: PhantomData<fn(&'a ()) -> &'a ()>,\n   310→    // Ensure `Context` is `!Send` and `!Sync` in order to allow\n   311→    // for future `!Send` and / or `!Sync` fields.\n   312→    _marker2: PhantomData<*mut ()>,\n   313→}\n   314→\n   315→impl<'a> ContextBuilder<'a> {\n   316→    /// Creates a ContextBuilder from a Waker.\n   317→    #[inline]\n   318→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   319→    pub const fn from_waker(waker: &'a Waker) -> Self {\n   320→        // SAFETY: LocalWaker is just Waker without thread safety\n   321→        let local_waker = unsafe { transmute(waker) };\n   322→        Self {\n   323→            waker,\n   324→            local_waker,\n   325→            ext: ExtData::None(()),\n   326→            _marker: PhantomData,\n   327→            _marker2: PhantomData,\n   328→        }\n   329→    }\n   330→\n   331→    /// Creates a ContextBuilder from an existing Context.\n   332→    #[inline]\n   333→    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n   334→    pub const fn from(cx: &'a mut Context<'_>) -> Self {\n   335→        let ext = match &mut cx.ext.0 {\n   336→            ExtData::Some(ext) => ExtData::Some(*ext),\n   337→            ExtData::None(()) => ExtData::None(()),\n   338→        };\n   339→        Self {\n   340→            waker: cx.waker,\n   341→            local_waker: cx.local_waker,\n   342→            ext,\n   343→            _marker: PhantomData,\n   344→            _marker2: PhantomData,\n   345→        }\n   346→    }\n   347→\n   348→    /// Sets the value for the waker on `Context`.\n   349→    #[inline]\n   350→    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n   351→    pub const fn waker(self, waker: &'a Waker) -> Self {\n   352→        Self { waker, ..self }\n   353→    }\n   354→\n   355→    /// Sets the value for the local waker on `Context`.\n   356→    #[inline]\n   357→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   358→    pub const fn local_waker(self, local_waker: &'a LocalWaker) -> Self {\n   359→        Self { local_waker, ..self }\n   360→    }\n   361→\n   362→    /// Sets the value for the extension data on `Context`.\n   363→    #[inline]\n   364→    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n   365→    pub const fn ext(self, data: &'a mut dyn Any) -> Self {\n   366→        Self { ext: ExtData::Some(data), ..self }\n   367→    }\n   368→\n   369→    /// Builds the `Context`.\n   370→    #[inline]\n   371→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   372→    pub const fn build(self) -> Context<'a> {\n   373→        let ContextBuilder { waker, local_waker, ext, _marker, _marker2 } = self;\n   374→        Context { waker, local_waker, ext: AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\n   375→    }\n   376→}\n   377→\n   378→/// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\n   379→/// is ready to be run.\n   380→///\n   381→/// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n   382→/// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n   383→///\n   384→/// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n   385→/// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n   386→/// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\n   387→/// the future should be polled again.\n   388→///\n   389→/// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\n   390→/// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\n   391→/// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\n   392→/// thread.\n   393→///\n   394→/// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n   395→/// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n   396→/// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n   397→///\n   398→/// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\n   399→/// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\n   400→///\n   401→/// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n   402→/// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n   403→/// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n   404→#[repr(transparent)]\n   405→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   406→#[rustc_diagnostic_item = \"Waker\"]\n   407→pub struct Waker {\n   408→    waker: RawWaker,\n   409→}\n   410→\n   411→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   412→impl Unpin for Waker {}\n   413→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   414→unsafe impl Send for Waker {}\n   415→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   416→unsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\n   417→\n   418→impl Waker {\n   419→    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\n   420→    ///\n   421→    /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n   422→    /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n   423→    /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n   424→    /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\n   425→    /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n   426→    /// unbounded processing loops.\n   427→    ///\n   428→    /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n   429→    /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n   430→    ///\n   431→    /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n   432→    /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n   433→    /// current task again.\n   434→    ///\n   435→    /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n   436→    #[inline]\n   437→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   438→    pub fn wake(self) {\n   439→        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n   440→        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n   441→\n   442→        // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n   443→        let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n   444→\n   445→        // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n   446→        // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n   447→        // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n   448→        unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n   449→    }\n   450→\n   451→    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\n   452→    ///\n   453→    /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n   454→    /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\n   455→    /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\n   456→    #[inline]\n   457→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   458→    pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\n   459→        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n   460→        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n   461→\n   462→        // SAFETY: see `wake`\n   463→        unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\n   464→    }\n   465→\n   466→    /// Returns `true` if this `Waker` and another `Waker` would awake the same task.\n   467→    ///\n   468→    /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\n   469→    /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\n   470→    /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n   471→    ///\n   472→    /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\n   473→    /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n   474→    /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n   475→    #[inline]\n   476→    #[must_use]\n   477→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   478→    pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &Waker) -> bool {\n   479→        // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n   480→        // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n   481→        let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n   482→        let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n   483→        a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n   484→    }\n   485→\n   486→    /// Creates a new `Waker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n   487→    ///\n   488→    /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n   489→    /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n   490→    /// that is associated with the task.\n   491→    /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n   492→    /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n   493→    ///\n   494→    /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n   495→    /// thread safe type such as an `Arc`.\n   496→    ///\n   497→    /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker`. For each operation\n   498→    /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\n   499→    ///\n   500→    /// # Safety\n   501→    ///\n   502→    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n   503→    /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n   504→    ///\n   505→    /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n   506→    /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n   507→    ///\n   508→    /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n   509→    #[inline]\n   510→    #[must_use]\n   511→    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n   512→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n   513→    pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n   514→        Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n   515→    }\n   516→\n   517→    /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\n   518→    ///\n   519→    /// # Safety\n   520→    ///\n   521→    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n   522→    /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n   523→    ///\n   524→    /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n   525→    /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n   526→    ///\n   527→    /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n   528→    #[inline]\n   529→    #[must_use]\n   530→    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   531→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n   532→    pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\n   533→        Waker { waker }\n   534→    }\n   535→\n   536→    /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\n   537→    ///\n   538→    // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\n   539→    // in the docs for `LocalWaker::noop`.\n   540→    // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\n   541→    //\n   542→    /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\n   543→    /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\n   544→    /// do not need to do anything specific if it happens.\n   545→    ///\n   546→    /// More generally, using `Waker::noop()` to poll a future\n   547→    /// means discarding the notification of when the future should be polled again.\n   548→    /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\n   549→    ///\n   550→    /// If an owned `Waker` is needed, `clone()` this one.\n   551→    ///\n   552→    /// # Examples\n   553→    ///\n   554→    /// ```\n   555→    /// use std::future::Future;\n   556→    /// use std::task;\n   557→    ///\n   558→    /// let mut cx = task::Context::from_waker(task::Waker::noop());\n   559→    ///\n   560→    /// let mut future = Box::pin(async { 10 });\n   561→    /// assert_eq!(future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx), task::Poll::Ready(10));\n   562→    /// ```\n   563→    #[inline]\n   564→    #[must_use]\n   565→    #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n   566→    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n   567→    pub const fn noop() -> &'static Waker {\n   568→        const WAKER: &Waker = &Waker { waker: RawWaker::NOOP };\n   569→        WAKER\n   570→    }\n   571→\n   572→    /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n   573→    #[inline]\n   574→    #[must_use]\n   575→    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n   576→    pub fn data(&self) -> *const () {\n   577→        self.waker.data\n   578→    }\n   579→\n   580→    /// Gets the `vtable` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n   581→    #[inline]\n   582→    #[must_use]\n   583→    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n   584→    pub fn vtable(&self) -> &'static RawWakerVTable {\n   585→        self.waker.vtable\n   586→    }\n   587→\n   588→    /// Constructs a `Waker` from a function pointer.\n   589→    #[inline]\n   590→    #[must_use]\n   591→    #[unstable(feature = \"waker_from_fn_ptr\", issue = \"148457\")]\n   592→    pub const fn from_fn_ptr(f: fn()) -> Self {\n   593→        // SAFETY: Unsafe is used for transmutes, pointer came from `fn()` so it\n   594→        //         is sound to transmute it back to `fn()`.\n   595→        static VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = unsafe {\n   596→            RawWakerVTable::new(\n   597→                |this| RawWaker::new(this, &VTABLE),\n   598→                |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n   599→                |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n   600→                |_| {},\n   601→            )\n   602→        };\n   603→        let raw = RawWaker::new(f as *const (), &VTABLE);\n   604→\n   605→        // SAFETY: `clone` is just a copy, `drop` is a no-op while `wake` and\n   606→        //         `wake_by_ref` just call the function pointer.\n   607→        unsafe { Self::from_raw(raw) }\n   608→    }\n   609→}\n   610→\n   611→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   612→impl Clone for Waker {\n   613→    #[inline]\n   614→    fn clone(&self) -> Self {\n   615→        Waker {\n   616→            // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n   617→            // to initialize `clone` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n   618→            // that the contract of [`RawWaker`] is upheld.\n   619→            waker: unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.clone)(self.waker.data) },\n   620→        }\n   621→    }\n   622→\n   623→    /// Assigns a clone of `source` to `self`, unless [`self.will_wake(source)`][Waker::will_wake] anyway.\n   624→    ///\n   625→    /// This method is preferred over simply assigning `source.clone()` to `self`,\n   626→    /// as it avoids cloning the waker if `self` is already the same waker.\n   627→    ///\n   628→    /// # Examples\n   629→    ///\n   630→    /// ```\n   631→    /// use std::future::Future;\n   632→    /// use std::pin::Pin;\n   633→    /// use std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\n   634→    /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Waker};\n   635→    ///\n   636→    /// struct Waiter {\n   637→    ///     shared: Arc<Mutex<Shared>>,\n   638→    /// }\n   639→    ///\n   640→    /// struct Shared {\n   641→    ///     waker: Waker,\n   642→    ///     // ...\n   643→    /// }\n   644→    ///\n   645→    /// impl Future for Waiter {\n   646→    ///     type Output = ();\n   647→    ///     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<()> {\n   648→    ///         let mut shared = self.shared.lock().unwrap();\n   649→    ///\n   650→    ///         // update the waker\n   651→    ///         shared.waker.clone_from(cx.waker());\n   652→    ///\n   653→    ///         // readiness logic ...\n   654→    /// #       Poll::Ready(())\n   655→    ///     }\n   656→    /// }\n   657→    ///\n   658→    /// ```\n   659→    #[inline]\n   660→    fn clone_from(&mut self, source: &Self) {\n   661→        if !self.will_wake(source) {\n   662→            *self = source.clone();\n   663→        }\n   664→    }\n   665→}\n   666→\n   667→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   668→impl Drop for Waker {\n   669→    #[inline]\n   670→    fn drop(&mut self) {\n   671→        // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n   672→        // to initialize `drop` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n   673→        // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n   674→        unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.drop)(self.waker.data) }\n   675→    }\n   676→}\n   677→\n   678→#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n   679→impl fmt::Debug for Waker {\n   680→    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n   681→        let vtable_ptr = self.waker.vtable as *const RawWakerVTable;\n   682→        f.debug_struct(\"Waker\")\n   683→            .field(\"data\", &self.waker.data)\n   684→            .field(\"vtable\", &vtable_ptr)\n   685→            .finish()\n   686→    }\n   687→}\n   688→\n   689→/// A `LocalWaker` is analogous to a [`Waker`], but it does not implement [`Send`] or [`Sync`].\n   690→///\n   691→/// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n   692→/// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n   693→///\n   694→/// Local wakers can be requested from a `Context` with the [`local_waker`] method.\n   695→///\n   696→/// The typical life of a `LocalWaker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n   697→/// [`Context`] using [`ContextBuilder`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n   698→/// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`LocalWaker::wake()`] when\n   699→/// the future should be polled again.\n   700→///\n   701→/// Implements [`Clone`], but neither [`Send`] nor [`Sync`]; therefore, a local waker may\n   702→/// not be moved to other threads. In general, when deciding to use wakers or local wakers,\n   703→/// local wakers are preferable unless the waker needs to be sent across threads. This is because\n   704→/// wakers can incur in additional cost related to memory synchronization.\n   705→///\n   706→/// Note that it is preferable to use `local_waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n   707→/// of `*local_waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n   708→/// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n   709→///\n   710→/// # Examples\n   711→/// Usage of a local waker to implement a future analogous to `std::thread::yield_now()`.\n   712→/// ```\n   713→/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n   714→/// use std::future::{Future, poll_fn};\n   715→/// use std::task::Poll;\n   716→///\n   717→/// // a future that returns pending once.\n   718→/// fn yield_now() -> impl Future<Output=()> + Unpin {\n   719→///     let mut yielded = false;\n   720→///     poll_fn(move |cx| {\n   721→///         if !yielded {\n   722→///             yielded = true;\n   723→///             cx.local_waker().wake_by_ref();\n   724→///             return Poll::Pending;\n   725→///         }\n   726→///         return Poll::Ready(())\n   727→///     })\n   728→/// }\n   729→///\n   730→/// # async fn __() {\n   731→/// yield_now().await;\n   732→/// # }\n   733→/// ```\n   734→///\n   735→/// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n   736→/// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n   737→/// [`local_waker`]: core::task::Context::local_waker\n   738→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   739→#[repr(transparent)]\n   740→pub struct LocalWaker {\n   741→    waker: RawWaker,\n   742→}\n   743→\n   744→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   745→impl Unpin for LocalWaker {}\n   746→\n   747→impl LocalWaker {\n   748→    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker`.\n   749→    ///\n   750→    /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n   751→    /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n   752→    /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n   753→    /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `LocalWaker` belongs. This makes\n   754→    /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n   755→    /// unbounded processing loops.\n   756→    ///\n   757→    /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n   758→    /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n   759→    ///\n   760→    /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n   761→    /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n   762→    /// current task again.\n   763→    ///\n   764→    /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n   765→    #[inline]\n   766→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   767→    pub fn wake(self) {\n   768→        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n   769→        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n   770→\n   771→        // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n   772→        let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n   773→\n   774→        // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n   775→        // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n   776→        // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n   777→        unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n   778→    }\n   779→\n   780→    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker` without consuming the `LocalWaker`.\n   781→    ///\n   782→    /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n   783→    /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\n   784→    /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\n   785→    #[inline]\n   786→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   787→    pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\n   788→        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n   789→        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n   790→\n   791→        // SAFETY: see `wake`\n   792→        unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\n   793→    }\n   794→\n   795→    /// Returns `true` if this `LocalWaker` and another `LocalWaker` would awake the same task.\n   796→    ///\n   797→    /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\n   798→    /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\n   799→    /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n   800→    ///\n   801→    /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\n   802→    /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n   803→    /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n   804→    #[inline]\n   805→    #[must_use]\n   806→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   807→    pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &LocalWaker) -> bool {\n   808→        // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n   809→        // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n   810→        let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n   811→        let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n   812→        a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n   813→    }\n   814→\n   815→    /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n   816→    ///\n   817→    /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n   818→    /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n   819→    /// that is associated with the task.\n   820→    /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n   821→    /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n   822→    ///\n   823→    /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `LocalWaker`. For each\n   824→    /// operation on the `LocalWaker`, the associated function in the `vtable`\n   825→    /// will be called.\n   826→    ///\n   827→    /// # Safety\n   828→    ///\n   829→    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n   830→    /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n   831→    ///\n   832→    #[inline]\n   833→    #[must_use]\n   834→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   835→    pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n   836→        LocalWaker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n   837→    }\n   838→\n   839→    /// Creates a new `LocalWaker` from [`RawWaker`].\n   840→    ///\n   841→    /// The behavior of the returned `LocalWaker` is undefined if the contract defined\n   842→    /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n   843→    /// Therefore this method is unsafe.\n   844→    #[inline]\n   845→    #[must_use]\n   846→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   847→    pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> LocalWaker {\n   848→        Self { waker }\n   849→    }\n   850→\n   851→    /// Returns a reference to a `LocalWaker` that does nothing when used.\n   852→    ///\n   853→    // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\n   854→    // in the docs for `Waker::noop`.\n   855→    // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\n   856→    //\n   857→    /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\n   858→    /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\n   859→    /// do not need to do anything specific if it happens.\n   860→    ///\n   861→    /// More generally, using `LocalWaker::noop()` to poll a future\n   862→    /// means discarding the notification of when the future should be polled again,\n   863→    /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\n   864→    ///\n   865→    /// If an owned `LocalWaker` is needed, `clone()` this one.\n   866→    ///\n   867→    /// # Examples\n   868→    ///\n   869→    /// ```\n   870→    /// #![feature(local_waker)]\n   871→    /// use std::future::Future;\n   872→    /// use std::task::{ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker, Poll};\n   873→    ///\n   874→    /// let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\n   875→    ///     .local_waker(LocalWaker::noop())\n   876→    ///     .build();\n   877→    ///\n   878→    /// let mut future = Box::pin(async { 10 });\n   879→    /// assert_eq!(future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx), Poll::Ready(10));\n   880→    /// ```\n   881→    #[inline]\n   882→    #[must_use]\n   883→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   884→    pub const fn noop() -> &'static LocalWaker {\n   885→        const WAKER: &LocalWaker = &LocalWaker { waker: RawWaker::NOOP };\n   886→        WAKER\n   887→    }\n   888→\n   889→    /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `LocalWaker`.\n   890→    #[inline]\n   891→    #[must_use]\n   892→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   893→    pub fn data(&self) -> *const () {\n   894→        self.waker.data\n   895→    }\n   896→\n   897→    /// Gets the `vtable` pointer used to create this `LocalWaker`.\n   898→    #[inline]\n   899→    #[must_use]\n   900→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   901→    pub fn vtable(&self) -> &'static RawWakerVTable {\n   902→        self.waker.vtable\n   903→    }\n   904→\n   905→    /// Constructs a `LocalWaker` from a function pointer.\n   906→    #[inline]\n   907→    #[must_use]\n   908→    #[unstable(feature = \"waker_from_fn_ptr\", issue = \"148457\")]\n   909→    pub const fn from_fn_ptr(f: fn()) -> Self {\n   910→        // SAFETY: Unsafe is used for RawWakerVTable::new(\n   914→                |this| RawWaker::new(this, &VTABLE),\n   915→                |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n   916→                |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n   917→                |_| {},\n   918→            )\n   919→        };\n   920→        let raw = RawWaker::new(f as *const (), &VTABLE);\n   921→\n   922→        // SAFETY: `clone` is just a copy, `drop` is a no-op while `wake` and\n   923→        //         `wake_by_ref` just call the function pointer.\n   924→        unsafe { Self::from_raw(raw) }\n   925→    }\n   926→}\n   927→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   928→impl Clone for LocalWaker {\n   929→    #[inline]\n   930→    fn clone(&self) -> Self {\n   931→        LocalWaker {\n clone_from(&mut self, source: &Self) {\n   941→        if !self.will_wake(source) {\n   942→            *self = source.clone();\n   943→        }\n   944→    }\n   945→}\n   946→\n   947→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   948→#[rustc_const_unstable(feature = \"const_convert\", issue = \"143773\")]\n   949→impl const AsRef<LocalWaker> for Waker {\n   950→    fn as_ref(&self) -> &LocalWaker {\n   951→        // SAFETY: LocalWaker is just Waker without thread safety\n   952→        unsafe { transmute(self) }\n   953→    }\n   954→}\n   955→\n This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n    /// that is associated with the task.\n    /// The value of this field gets passed to all functions that are part of\n    /// the vtable as the first parameter.\n    data: *const (),\n    /// Virtual function pointer table that customizes the behavior of this waker.\n    vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable,\n}\n\nimpl RawWaker {\n    /// Creates a new `RawWaker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n    ///\n    /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n    /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n    /// that is associated with the task.\n    /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n    /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n    ///\n    /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n    /// thread safe type such as an `Arc<T: Send + Sync>`\n    /// when used to construct a [`Waker`]. This restriction is lifted when\n    /// constructing a [`LocalWaker`], which allows using types that do not implement\n    /// <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code> like `Rc<T>`.\n    ///\n    /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker` which gets created\n    /// from a `RawWaker`. For each operation on the `Waker`, the associated\n    /// function in the `vtable` of the underlying `RawWaker` will be called.\n    #[inline]\n    #[rustc_promotable]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[must_use]\n    pub const fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> RawWaker {\n        RawWaker { data, vtable }\n    }\n\n    #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n    const NOOP: RawWaker = {\n        const VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = RawWakerVTable::new(\n            // Cloning just returns a new no-op raw waker\n            |_| RawWaker::NOOP,\n            // `wake` does nothing\n            |_| {},\n            // `wake_by_ref` does nothing\n            |_| {},\n            // Dropping does nothing as we don't allocate anything\n            |_| {},\n        );\n        RawWaker::new(ptr::null(), &VTABLE)\n    };\n}\n\n/// A virtual function pointer table (vtable) that specifies the behavior\n/// of a [`RawWaker`].\n///\n/// The pointer passed to all functions inside the vtable is the `data` pointer\n/// from the enclosing [`RawWaker`] object.\n///\n/// The functions inside this struct are only intended to be called on the `data`\n/// pointer of a properly constructed [`RawWaker`] object from inside the\n/// [`RawWaker`] implementation. Calling one of the contained functions using\n/// any other `data` pointer will cause undefined behavior.\n///\n/// Note that while this type implements `PartialEq`, comparing function pointers, and hence\n/// comparing structs like this that contain function pointers, is unreliable: pointers to the same\n/// function can compare inequal (because functions are duplicated in multiple codegen units), and\n/// pointers to *different* functions can compare equal (since identical functions can be\n/// deduplicated within a codegen unit).\n///\n/// # Thread safety\n/// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\n/// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\n/// <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\n/// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\n/// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\n/// they must do so atomically.\n///\n/// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\n/// these functions don't need to be thread safe. This means that <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>\n///  data can be stored in the data pointer, and reference counting does not need any atomic\n/// synchronization. This is because [`LocalWaker`] is not thread safe itself, so it cannot\n/// be sent across threads.\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n#[allow(unpredictable_function_pointer_comparisons)]\n#[derive(PartialEq, Copy, Clone, Debug)]\npub struct RawWakerVTable {\n    /// This function will be called when the [`RawWaker`] gets cloned, e.g. when\n    /// the [`Waker`] in which the [`RawWaker`] is stored gets cloned.\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must retain all resources that are\n    /// required for this additional instance of a [`RawWaker`] and associated\n    /// task. Calling `wake` on the resulting [`RawWaker`] should result in a wakeup\n    /// of the same task that would have been awoken by the original [`RawWaker`].\n    clone: unsafe fn(*const ()) -> RawWaker,\n\n    /// This function will be called when `wake` is called on the [`Waker`].\n    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n    /// associated task.\n    wake: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n\n    /// This function will be called when `wake_by_ref` is called on the [`Waker`].\n    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// This function is similar to `wake`, but must not consume the provided data\n    /// pointer.\n    wake_by_ref: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n\n    /// This function will be called when a [`Waker`] gets dropped.\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n    /// associated task.\n    drop: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n}\n\nimpl RawWakerVTable {\n    /// Creates a new `RawWakerVTable` from the provided `clone`, `wake`,\n    /// `wake_by_ref`, and `drop` functions.\n    ///\n    /// If the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`Waker`] then\n    /// these functions must all be thread-safe (even though [`RawWaker`] is\n    /// <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>). This is because [`Waker`] is <code>[Send] + [Sync]</code>,\n    /// and it may be moved to arbitrary threads or invoked by `&` reference. For example,\n    /// this means that if the `clone` and `drop` functions manage a reference count,\n    /// they must do so atomically.\n    ///\n    /// However, if the [`RawWaker`] will be used to construct a [`LocalWaker`] instead, then\n    /// these functions don't need to be thread safe. This means that <code>\\![Send] + \\![Sync]</code>\n    /// data can be stored in the data pointer, and reference counting does not need any atomic\n    /// synchronization. This is because [`LocalWaker`] is not thread safe itself, so it cannot\n    /// be sent across threads.\n    /// # `clone`\n    ///\n    /// This function will be called when the [`RawWaker`] gets cloned, e.g. when\n    /// the [`Waker`]/[`LocalWaker`] in which the [`RawWaker`] is stored gets cloned.\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must retain all resources that are\n    /// required for this additional instance of a [`RawWaker`] and associated\n    /// task. Calling `wake` on the resulting [`RawWaker`] should result in a wakeup\n    /// of the same task that would have been awoken by the original [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// # `wake`\n    ///\n    /// This function will be called when `wake` is called on the [`Waker`].\n    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n    /// associated task.\n    ///\n    /// # `wake_by_ref`\n    ///\n    /// This function will be called when `wake_by_ref` is called on the [`Waker`].\n    /// It must wake up the task associated with this [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// This function is similar to `wake`, but must not consume the provided data\n    /// pointer.\n    ///\n    /// # `drop`\n    ///\n    /// This function will be called when a [`Waker`]/[`LocalWaker`] gets\n    /// dropped.\n    ///\n    /// The implementation of this function must make sure to release any\n    /// resources that are associated with this instance of a [`RawWaker`] and\n    /// associated task.\n    #[rustc_promotable]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    pub const fn new(\n        clone: unsafe fn(*const ()) -> RawWaker,\n        wake: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n        wake_by_ref: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n        drop: unsafe fn(*const ()),\n    ) -> Self {\n        Self { clone, wake, wake_by_ref, drop }\n    }\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug)]\nenum ExtData<'a> {\n    Some(&'a mut dyn Any),\n    None(()),\n}\n\n/// The context of an asynchronous task.\n///\n/// Currently, `Context` only serves to provide access to a [`&Waker`](Waker)\n/// which can be used to wake the current task.\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n#[lang = \"Context\"]\npub struct Context<'a> {\n    waker: &'a Waker,\n #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[inline]\n    pub const fn from_waker(waker:   }\n\n    /// Returns a reference to the [`LocalWaker`] for the current task.\n    #[inline]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n    pub const fn local_waker(&self) -> \"123392\")]\n    pub const fn ext(&mut self) -> &mut dyn Any {\n        // FIXME: this field makes Context extra-weird about unwind safety\n        // can we justify AssertUnwindSafe if we stabilize this? do we care?\n        match &mut self.ext.0 {\n            ExtData::Some(data) => *data,\n            ExtData::None(unit) => unit,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl fmt::Debug for Context<'_> {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        f.debug_struct(\"Context\").field(\"waker\", &self.waker).finish()\n    }\n}\n\n/// A Builder used to construct a `Context` instance\n/// with support for `LocalWaker`.\n///\n/// # Examples\n/// ```\n/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n/// use std::task::{ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker, Poll};\n/// use std::future::Future;\n///\n/// let local_waker = LocalWaker::noop();\n/// let waker = Waker::noop();\n///\n/// let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(&waker)\n/// LocalWaker,\n    ext: ExtData<'a>,\n    // Ensure we future-proof against variance changes by forcing\n    // the lifetime to be invariant (argument-position lifetimes\n    // are contravariant while return-position lifetimes are\n    // covariant).\n    _marker: PhantomData<fn(&'a ()) -> &'a ()>,\n    // Ensure `Context` is `!Send` and `!Sync` in order to allow\n    // for future `!Send` and / or `!Sync` fields.\n    _marker2: PhantomData<*mut ()>,\n}\n\nimpl<'a> ContextBuilder<'a> {\n    /// Creates a ContextBuilder from a Waker.\n    #[inline]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n    pub const fn from_waker(waker: &'a Waker) -> Self {\n        // SAFETY: LocalWaker is just Waker without thread safety\n        let local_waker = unsafe { transmute(waker) };\n        Self {\n            waker,\n            local_waker,\n            ext: ExtData::None(()),\n            _marker: PhantomData,\n            _marker2: PhantomData,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Creates a ContextBuilder from an existing Context.\n    #[inline]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n    pub const fn from(cx: &'a mut Context<'_>) -> Self {\n        let ext = match &mut cx.ext.0 {\n            ExtData::Some(ext) => ExtData::Some(*ext),\n            ExtData::None(()) => ExtData::None(()),\n        };\n        Self {\n            waker: cx.waker,\n            local_waker: cx.local_waker,\n            ext,\n            _marker: PhantomData,\n            _marker2: PhantomData,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Sets the value for the waker on `Context`.\n    #[inline]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n    pub const fn waker(self, waker: &'a Waker) -> Self {\n        Self { waker, ..self }\n    }\n\n    /// Sets the value for the local waker on `Context`.\n    #[inline]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n    pub const fn local_waker(self, local_waker: &'a LocalWaker) -> Self {\n        Self { local_waker, ..self }\n    }\n\n    /// Sets the value for the extension data on `Context`.\n    #[inline]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"context_ext\", issue = \"123392\")]\n    pub const fn ext(self, data: &'a mut dyn Any) -> Self {\n        Self { ext: ExtData::Some(data), ..self }\n    }\n\n    /// Builds the `Context`.\n    #[inline]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n    pub const fn build(self) -> Context<'a> {\n        let ContextBuilder { waker, local_waker, ext, _marker, _marker2 } = self;\n        Context { waker, local_waker, ext: AssertUnwindSafe(ext), _marker, _marker2 }\n    }\n}\n\n/// A `Waker` is a handle for waking up a task by notifying its executor that it\n/// is ready to be run.\n///\n/// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n/// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n///\n/// The typical life of a `Waker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n/// [`Context`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n/// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`Waker::wake()`] when\n/// the future should be polled again.\n///\n/// Implements [`Clone`], [`Send`], and [`Sync`]; therefore, a waker may be invoked\n/// from any thread, including ones not in any way managed by the executor. For example,\n/// this might be done to wake a future when a blocking function call completes on another\n/// thread.\n///\n/// Note that it is preferable to use `waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n/// of `*waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n/// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n///\n/// Constructing a `Waker` from a [`RawWaker`] is unsafe.\n/// Implementing the [`Wake`] trait is a safe alternative that requires memory allocation.\n///\n/// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n/// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n/// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n#[repr(transparent)]\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n#[rustc_diagnostic_item = \"Waker\"]\npub struct Waker {\n    waker: RawWaker,\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl Unpin for Waker {}\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nunsafe impl Send for Waker {}\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nunsafe impl Sync for Waker {}\n\nimpl Waker {\n    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker`.\n    ///\n    /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n    /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n    /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n    /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `Waker` belongs. This makes\n    /// it possible to temporarily yield to other tasks while running potentially\n    /// unbounded processing loops.\n    ///\n    /// Note that the above implies that multiple wake-ups may be coalesced into a\n    /// single [`poll()`] invocation by the runtime.\n    ///\n    /// Also note that yielding to competing tasks is not guaranteed: it is the\n    /// executor’s choice which task to run and the executor may choose to run the\n    /// current task again.\n    ///\n    /// [`poll()`]: crate::future::Future::poll\n    #[inline]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    pub fn wake(self) {\n        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n\n        // Don't call `drop` -- the waker will be consumed by `wake`.\n        let this = ManuallyDrop::new(self);\n\n        // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n        // to initialize `wake` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n        // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n        unsafe { (this.waker.vtable.wake)(this.waker.data) };\n    }\n\n    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `Waker` without consuming the `Waker`.\n    ///\n    /// This is similar to [`wake()`](Self::wake), but may be slightly less efficient in\n    /// the case where an owned `Waker` is available. This method should be preferred to\n    /// calling `waker.clone().wake()`.\n    #[inline]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    pub fn wake_by_ref(&self) {\n        // The actual wakeup call is delegated through a virtual function call\n        // to the implementation which is defined by the executor.\n\n        // SAFETY: see `wake`\n        unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.wake_by_ref)(self.waker.data) }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns `true` if this `Waker` and another `Waker` would awake the same task.\n    ///\n    /// This function works on a best-effort basis, and may return false even\n    /// when the `Waker`s would awaken the same task. However, if this function\n    /// returns `true`, it is guaranteed that the `Waker`s will awaken the same task.\n    ///\n    /// This function is primarily used for optimization purposes — for example,\n    /// this type's [`clone_from`](Self::clone_from) implementation uses it to\n    /// avoid cloning the waker when they would wake the same task anyway.\n    #[inline]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    pub fn will_wake(&self, other: &Waker) -> bool {\n        // We optimize this by comparing vtable addresses instead of vtable contents.\n        // This is permitted since the function is documented as best-effort.\n        let RawWaker { data: a_data, vtable: a_vtable } = self.waker;\n        let RawWaker { data: b_data, vtable: b_vtable } = other.waker;\n        a_data == b_data && ptr::eq(a_vtable, b_vtable)\n    }\n\n    /// Creates a new `Waker` from the provided `data` pointer and `vtable`.\n    ///\n    /// The `data` pointer can be used to store arbitrary data as required\n    /// by the executor. This could be e.g. a type-erased pointer to an `Arc`\n    /// that is associated with the task.\n    /// The value of this pointer will get passed to all functions that are part\n    /// of the `vtable` as the first parameter.\n    ///\n    /// It is important to consider that the `data` pointer must point to a\n    /// thread safe type such as an `Arc`.\n    ///\n    /// The `vtable` customizes the behavior of a `Waker`. For each operation\n    /// on the `Waker`, the associated function in the `vtable` will be called.\n    ///\n    /// # Safety\n    ///\n    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n    /// in [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n    ///\n    /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n    /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n    ///\n    /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n    #[inline]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n    pub const unsafe fn new(data: *const (), vtable: &'static RawWakerVTable) -> Self {\n        Waker { waker: RawWaker { data, vtable } }\n    }\n\n    /// Creates a new `Waker` from [`RawWaker`].\n    ///\n    /// # Safety\n    ///\n    /// The behavior of the returned `Waker` is undefined if the contract defined\n    /// in [`RawWaker`]'s and [`RawWakerVTable`]'s documentation is not upheld.\n    ///\n    /// (Authors wishing to avoid unsafe code may implement the [`Wake`] trait instead, at the\n    /// cost of a required heap allocation.)\n    ///\n    /// [`Wake`]: ../../alloc/task/trait.Wake.html\n    #[inline]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"const_waker\", since = \"1.82.0\")]\n    pub const unsafe fn from_raw(waker: RawWaker) -> Waker {\n        Waker { waker }\n    }\n\n    /// Returns a reference to a `Waker` that does nothing when used.\n    ///\n    // Note!  Much of the documentation for this method is duplicated\n    // in the docs for `LocalWaker::noop`.\n    // If you edit it, consider editing the other copy too.\n    //\n    /// This is mostly useful for writing tests that need a [`Context`] to poll\n    /// some futures, but are not expecting those futures to wake the waker or\n    /// do not need to do anything specific if it happens.\n    ///\n    /// More generally, using `Waker::noop()` to poll a future\n    /// means discarding the notification of when the future should be polled again.\n    /// So it should only be used when such a notification will not be needed to make progress.\n    ///\n    /// If an owned `Waker` is needed, `clone()` this one.\n    ///\n    /// # Examples\n    ///\n    /// ```\n    /// use std::future::Future;\n    /// use std::task;\n    ///\n    /// let mut cx = task::Context::from_waker(task::Waker::noop());\n    ///\n    /// let mut future = Box::pin(async { 10 });\n    /// assert_eq!(future.as_mut().poll(&mut cx), task::Poll::Ready(10));\n    /// ```\n    #[inline]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n    #[rustc_const_stable(feature = \"noop_waker\", since = \"1.85.0\")]\n    pub const fn noop() -> &'static Waker {\n        const WAKER: &Waker = &Waker { waker: RawWaker::NOOP };\n        WAKER\n    }\n\n    /// Gets the `data` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n    #[inline]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n    pub fn data(&self) -> *const () {\n        self.waker.data\n    }\n\n    /// Gets the `vtable` pointer used to create this `Waker`.\n    #[inline]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[stable(feature = \"waker_getters\", since = \"1.83.0\")]\n    pub fn vtable(&self) -> &'static RawWakerVTable {\n        self.waker.vtable\n    }\n\n    /// Constructs a `Waker` from a function pointer.\n    #[inline]\n    #[must_use]\n    #[unstable(feature = \"waker_from_fn_ptr\", issue = \"148457\")]\n    pub const fn from_fn_ptr(f: fn()) -> Self {\n        // SAFETY: Unsafe is used for transmutes, pointer came from `fn()` so it\n        //         is sound to transmute it back to `fn()`.\n        static VTABLE: RawWakerVTable = unsafe {\n            RawWakerVTable::new(\n                |this| RawWaker::new(this, &VTABLE),\n                |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n                |this| transmute::<*const (), fn()>(this)(),\n                |_| {},\n            )\n        };\n        let raw = RawWaker::new(f as *const (), &VTABLE);\n\n        // SAFETY: `clone` is just a copy, `drop` is a no-op while `wake` and\n        //         `wake_by_ref` just call the function pointer.\n        unsafe { Self::from_raw(raw) }\n    }\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl Clone for Waker {\n    #[inline]\n    fn clone(&self) -> Self {\n        Waker {\n            // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n            // to initialize `clone` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n            // that the contract of [`RawWaker`] is upheld.\n            waker: unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.clone)(self.waker.data) },\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Assigns a clone of `source` to `self`, unless [`self.will_wake(source)`][Waker::will_wake] anyway.\n    ///\n    /// This method is preferred over simply assigning `source.clone()` to `self`,\n    /// as it avoids cloning the waker if `self` is already the same waker.\n    ///\n    /// # Examples\n    ///\n    /// ```\n    /// use std::future::Future;\n    /// use std::pin::Pin;\n    /// use std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\n    /// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Waker};\n    ///\n    /// struct Waiter {\n    ///     shared: Arc<Mutex<Shared>>,\n    /// }\n    ///\n    /// struct Shared {\n    ///     waker: Waker,\n    ///     // ...\n    /// }\n    ///\n    /// impl Future for Waiter {\n    ///     type Output = ();\n    ///     fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<()> {\n    ///         let mut shared = self.shared.lock().unwrap();\n    ///\n    ///         // update the waker\n    ///         shared.waker.clone_from(cx.waker());\n    ///\n    ///         // readiness logic ...\n    /// #       Poll::Ready(())\n    ///     }\n    /// }\n    ///\n    /// ```\n    #[inline]\n    fn clone_from(&mut self, source: &Self) {\n        if !self.will_wake(source) {\n            *self = source.clone();\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl Drop for Waker {\n    #[inline]\n    fn drop(&mut self) {\n        // SAFETY: This is safe because `Waker::from_raw` is the only way\n        // to initialize `drop` and `data` requiring the user to acknowledge\n        // that the contract of `RawWaker` is upheld.\n        unsafe { (self.waker.vtable.drop)(self.waker.data) }\n    }\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl fmt::Debug for Waker {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        let vtable_ptr = self.waker.vtable as *const RawWakerVTable;\n        f.debug_struct(\"Waker\")\n            .field(\"data\", &self.waker.data)\n            .field(\"vtable\", &vtable_ptr)\n            .finish()\n    }\n}\n\n/// A `LocalWaker` is analogous to a [`Waker`], but it does not implement [`Send`] or [`Sync`].\n///\n/// This handle encapsulates a [`RawWaker`] instance, which defines the\n/// executor-specific wakeup behavior.\n///\n/// Local wakers can be requested from a `Context` with the [`local_waker`] method.\n///\n/// The typical life of a `LocalWaker` is that it is constructed by an executor, wrapped in a\n/// [`Context`] using [`ContextBuilder`], then passed to [`Future::poll()`]. Then, if the future chooses to return\n/// [`Poll::Pending`], it must also store the waker somehow and call [`LocalWaker::wake()`] when\n/// the future should be polled again.\n///\n/// Implements [`Clone`], but neither [`Send`] nor [`Sync`]; therefore, a local waker may\n/// not be moved to other threads. In general, when deciding to use wakers or local wakers,\n/// local wakers are preferable unless the waker needs to be sent across threads. This is because\n/// wakers can incur in additional cost related to memory synchronization.\n///\n/// Note that it is preferable to use `local_waker.clone_from(&new_waker)` instead\n/// of `*local_waker = new_waker.clone()`, as the former will avoid cloning the waker\n/// unnecessarily if the two wakers [wake the same task](Self::will_wake).\n///\n/// # Examples\n/// Usage of a local waker to implement a future analogous to `std::thread::yield_now()`.\n/// ```\n/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n/// use std::future::{Future, poll_fn};\n/// use std::task::Poll;\n///\n/// // a future that returns pending once.\n/// fn yield_now() -> impl Future<Output=()> + Unpin {\n///     let mut yielded = false;\n///     poll_fn(move |cx| {\n///         if !yielded {\n///             yielded = true;\n///             cx.local_waker().wake_by_ref();\n///             return Poll::Pending;\n///         }\n///         return Poll::Ready(())\n///     })\n/// }\n///\n/// # async fn __() {\n/// yield_now().await;\n/// # }\n/// ```\n///\n/// [`Future::poll()`]: core::future::Future::poll\n/// [`Poll::Pending`]: core::task::Poll::Pending\n/// [`local_waker`]: core::task::Context::local_waker\n#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n#[repr(transparent)]\npub struct LocalWaker {\n    waker: RawWaker,\n}\n\n#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\nimpl Unpin for LocalWaker {}\n\nimpl LocalWaker {\n    /// Wakes up the task associated with this `LocalWaker`.\n    ///\n    /// As long as the executor keeps running and the task is not finished, it is\n    /// guaranteed that each invocation of [`wake()`](Self::wake) (or\n    /// [`wake_by_ref()`](Self::wake_by_ref)) will be followed by at least one\n    /// [`poll()`] of the task to which this `LocalWaker` belongs. This kind of\n/// \"asynchronous value\" makes it possible for a thread to continue doing useful\n/// work while it waits for the value to become available.\n///\n/// # The `poll` method\n///\n/// The core method of future, `poll`, *attempts* to resolve the future into a\n/// final value. This method does not block if the value is not ready. Instead,\n/// the current task is scheduled to be woken up when it's possible to make\n/// further progress by `poll`ing again. The `context` passed to the `poll`\n/// method can provide a [`Waker`], which is a handle for waking up the current\n/// task.\n///\n/// When using a future, you generally won't call `poll` directly, but instead\n/// `.await` the value.\n///\n/// [`async`]: ../../std/keyword.async.html\n/// [`Waker`]: crate::task::Waker\n#[doc(notable_trait)]\n#[doc(search_unbox)]\n#[must_use = \"futures do nothing unless you `.await` or poll them\"]\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n#[lang = \"future_trait\"]\n#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(\n    label = \"`{Self}` is not a future\",\n    message = \"`{Self}` is not a future\"\n)]\npub trait Future {\n    /// The type of value produced on completion.\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    #[lang = \"future_output\"]\n    type Output;\n\n    /// Attempts to resolve the future to a final value, registering\n    /// the current task for wakeup if the value is not yet available.\n    ///\n    /// # Return value\n    ///\n    /// This function returns:\n    ///\n    /// - [`Poll::Pending`] if the future is not ready yet\n    /// - [`Poll::Ready(val)`] with the result `val` of this future if it\n    ///   finished successfully.\n    ///\n    /// Once a future has finished, clients should not `poll` it again.\n    ///\n    /// When a future is not ready yet, `poll` returns `Poll::Pending` and\n    /// stores a clone of the [`Waker`] copied from the current [`Context`].\n    /// This [`Waker`] is then woken once the future can make progress.\n    /// For example, a future waiting for a socket to become\n    /// readable would call `.clone()` on the [`Waker`] and store it.\n    /// When a signal arrives elsewhere indicating that the socket is readable,\n    /// [`Waker::wake`] is called and the socket future's task is awoken.\n    /// Once a task has been woken up, it should attempt to `poll` the future\n    /// again, which may or may not produce a final value.\n    ///\n    /// Note that on multiple calls to `poll`, only the [`Waker`] from the\n    /// [`Context`] passed to the most recent call should be scheduled to\n    /// receive a wakeup.\n    ///\n    /// # Runtime characteristics\n    ///\n    /// Futures alone are *inert*; they must be *actively* `poll`ed for the\n    /// underlying computation to make progress, meaning that each time the\n    /// current task is woken up, it should actively re-`poll` pending futures\n    /// that it still has an interest in.\n    ///\n    /// Having said that, some Futures may represent a value that is being\n    /// computed in a different task. In this case, the future's underlying\n    /// computation is simply acting as a conduit for a value being computed\n    /// by that other task, which will proceed independently of the Future.\n    /// Futures of this kind are typically obtained when spawning a new task into an\n    /// async runtime.\n    ///\n    /// The `poll` function should not be called repeatedly in a tight loop --\n    /// instead, it should only be called when the future indicates that it is\n    /// ready to make progress (by calling `wake()`). If you're familiar with the\n    /// `poll(2)` or `select(2)` syscalls on Unix it's worth noting that futures\n    /// typically do *not* suffer the same problems of \"all wakeups must poll\n    /// all events\"; they are more like `epoll(4)`.\n    ///\n    /// An implementation of `poll` should strive to return quickly, and should\n    /// not block. Returning quickly prevents unnecessarily clogging up\n    /// threads or event loops. If it is known ahead of time that a call to\n    /// `poll` may end up taking a while, the work should be offloaded to a\n    /// thread pool (or something similar) to ensure that `poll` can return\n    /// quickly.\n    ///\n    /// # Panics\n    ///\n    /// Once a future has completed (returned `Ready` from `poll`), calling its\n    /// `poll` method again may panic, block forever, or cause other kinds of\n    /// problems; the `Future` trait places no requirements on the effects of\n    /// such a call. However, as the `poll` method is not marked `unsafe`,\n    /// Rust's usual rules apply: calls must never cause undefined behavior\n    /// (memory corruption, incorrect use of `unsafe` functions, or the like),\n    /// regardless of the future's state.\n    ///\n    /// [`Poll::Ready(val)`]: Poll::Ready\n    /// [`Waker`]: crate::task::Waker\n    /// [`Waker::wake`]: crate::task::Waker::wake\n    #[lang = \"poll\"]\n    #[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\n    fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output>;\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl<F: ?Sized + Future + Unpin> Future for &mut F {\n    type Output = F::Output;\n\n    fn poll(mut self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\n        F::poll(Pin::new(&mut **self), cx)\n    }\n}\n\n#[stable(feature = \"futures_api\", since = \"1.36.0\")]\nimpl<P> Future for Pin<P>\nwhere\n    P: ops::DerefMut<Target: Future>,\n{\n    type Output = <<P as ops::Deref>::Target as Future>::Output;\n\n    fn poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output> {\n        <P::Target as Future>::poll(self.as_deref_mut(), cx)\n    }\n}\n","numLines":136,"startLine":1,"totalLines":136}}}
