{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_019EmEE9LyLDmugCiGMwj2xh","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→#![stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n     2→\n     3→//! Types and Traits for working with asynchronous tasks.\n     4→//!\n     5→//! **Note**: Some of the types in this module are only available\n     6→//! on platforms that support atomic loads and stores of pointers.\n     7→//! This may be detected at compile time using\n     8→//! `#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]`.\n     9→\n    10→use core::mem::ManuallyDrop;\n    11→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n    12→use core::task::Waker;\n    13→use core::task::{LocalWaker, RawWaker, RawWakerVTable};\n    14→\n    15→use crate::rc::Rc;\n    16→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n    17→use crate::sync::Arc;\n    18→\n    19→/// The implementation of waking a task on an executor.\n    20→///\n    21→/// This trait can be used to create a [`Waker`]. An executor can define an\n    22→/// implementation of this trait, and use that to construct a [`Waker`] to pass\n    23→/// to the tasks that are executed on that executor.\n    24→///\n    25→/// This trait is a memory-safe and ergonomic alternative to constructing a\n    26→/// [`RawWaker`]. It supports the common executor design in which the data used\n    27→/// to wake up a task is stored in an [`Arc`]. Some executors (especially\n    28→/// those for embedded systems) cannot use this API, which is why [`RawWaker`]\n    29→/// exists as an alternative for those systems.\n    30→///\n    31→/// To construct a [`Waker`] from some type `W` implementing this trait,\n    32→/// wrap it in an [`Arc<W>`](Arc) and call `Waker::from()` on that.\n    33→/// It is also possible to convert to [`RawWaker`] in the same way.\n    34→///\n    35→/// <!-- Ideally we'd link to the `From` impl, but rustdoc doesn't generate any page for it within\n    36→///      `alloc` because `alloc` neither defines nor re-exports `From` or `Waker`, and we can't\n    37→///      link ../../std/task/struct.Waker.html#impl-From%3CArc%3CW,+Global%3E%3E-for-Waker\n    38→///      without getting a link-checking error in CI. -->\n    39→///\n    40→/// # Examples\n    41→///\n    42→/// A basic `block_on` function that takes a future and runs it to completion on\n    43→/// the current thread.\n    44→///\n    45→/// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. In order to prevent\n    46→/// deadlocks, production-grade implementations will also need to handle\n    47→/// intermediate calls to `thread::unpark` as well as nested invocations.\n    48→///\n    49→/// ```rust\n    50→/// use std::future::Future;\n    51→/// use std::sync::Arc;\n    52→/// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Wake};\n    53→/// use std::thread::{self, Thread};\n    54→/// use core::pin::pin;\n    55→///\n    56→/// /// A waker that wakes up the current thread when called.\n    57→/// struct ThreadWaker(Thread);\n    58→///\n    59→/// impl Wake for ThreadWaker {\n    60→///     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>) {\n    61→///         self.0.unpark();\n    62→///     }\n    63→/// }\n    64→///\n    65→/// /// Run a future to completion on the current thread.\n    66→/// fn block_on<T>(fut: impl Future<Output = T>) -> T {\n    67→///     // Pin the future so it can be polled.\n    68→///     let mut fut = pin!(fut);\n    69→///\n    70→///     // Create a new context to be passed to the future.\n    71→///     let t = thread::current();\n    72→///     let waker = Arc::new(ThreadWaker(t)).into();\n    73→///     let mut cx = Context::from_waker(&waker);\n    74→///\n    75→///     // Run the future to completion.\n    76→///     loop {\n    77→///         match fut.as_mut().poll(&mut cx) {\n    78→///             Poll::Ready(res) => return res,\n    79→///             Poll::Pending => thread::park(),\n    80→///         }\n    81→///     }\n    82→/// }\n    83→///\n    84→/// block_on(async {\n    85→///     println!(\"Hi from inside a future!\");\n    86→/// });\n    87→/// ```\n    88→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n    89→#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n    90→pub trait Wake {\n    91→    /// Wake this task.\n    92→    #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n    93→    fn wake(self: Arc<Self>);\n    94→\n    95→    /// Wake this task without consuming the waker.\n    96→    ///\n    97→    /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\n    98→    /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\n    99→    /// [`Arc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\n   100→    ///\n   101→    /// [`wake`]: Wake::wake\n   102→    #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n   103→    fn wake_by_ref(self: &Arc<Self>) {\n   104→        self.clone().wake();\n   105→    }\n   106→}\n   107→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n   108→#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n   109→impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for Waker {\n   110→    /// Use a [`Wake`]-able type as a `Waker`.\n   111→    ///\n   112→    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n   113→    fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> Waker {\n   114→        // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\n   115→        // a RawWaker from Arc<W>.\n   116→        unsafe { Waker::from_raw(raw_waker(waker)) }\n   117→    }\n   118→}\n   119→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n   120→#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n   121→impl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker {\n   122→    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\n   123→    ///\n   124→    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n   125→    fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n   126→        raw_waker(waker)\n   127→    }\n   128→}\n   129→\n   130→// NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\n   131→// inlining this into the `From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\n   132→// the safety of `From<Arc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\n   133→// trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\n   134→// explicitly.\n   135→#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n   136→#[inline(always)]\n   137→fn raw_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n   138→    // Increment the reference count of the arc to clone it.\n   139→    //\n   140→    // The #[inline(always)] is to ensure that raw_waker and clone_waker are\n   141→    // always generated in the same code generation unit as one another, and\n   142→    // therefore that the structurally identical const-promoted RawWakerVTable\n   143→    // within both functions is deduplicated at LLVM IR code generation time.\n   144→    // This allows optimizing Waker::will_wake to a single pointer comparison of\n   145→    // the vtable pointers, rather than comparing all four function pointers\n   146→    // within the vtables.\n   147→    #[inline(always)]\n   148→    unsafe fn clone_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\n   149→        unsafe { Arc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n   150→        RawWaker::new(\n   151→            waker,\n   152→            &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n   153→        )\n   154→    }\n   155→\n   156→    // Wake by value, moving the Arc into the Wake::wake function\n   157→    unsafe fn wake<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n   158→        let waker = unsafe { Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\n   159→        <W as Wake>::wake(waker);\n   160→    }\n   161→\n   162→    // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\n   163→    unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n   164→        let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\n   165→        <W as Wake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\n   166→    }\n   167→\n   168→    // Decrement the reference count of the Arc on drop\n   169→    unsafe fn drop_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n   170→        unsafe { Arc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n   171→    }\n   172→\n   173→    RawWaker::new(\n   174→        Arc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\n   175→        &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n   176→    )\n   177→}\n   178→\n   179→/// An analogous trait to `Wake` but used to construct a `LocalWaker`.\n   180→///\n   181→/// This API works in exactly the same way as `Wake`,\n   182→/// except that it uses an `Rc` instead of an `Arc`,\n   183→/// and the result is a `LocalWaker` instead of a `Waker`.\n   184→///\n   185→/// The benefits of using `LocalWaker` over `Waker` are that it allows the local waker\n   186→/// to hold data that does not implement `Send` and `Sync`. Additionally, it saves calls\n   187→/// to `Arc::clone`, which requires atomic synchronization.\n   188→///\n   189→///\n   190→/// # Examples\n   191→///\n   192→/// This is a simplified example of a `spawn` and a `block_on` function. The `spawn` function\n   193→/// is used to push new tasks onto the run queue, while the block on function will remove them\n   194→/// and poll them. When a task is woken, it will put itself back on the run queue to be polled\n   195→/// by the executor.\n   196→///\n   197→/// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. A real world example would interleave\n   198→/// poll calls with calls to an io reactor to wait for events instead of spinning on a loop.\n   199→///\n   200→/// ```rust\n   201→/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n   202→/// use std::task::{LocalWake, ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker};\n   203→/// use std::future::Future;\n   204→/// use std::pin::Pin;\n   205→/// use std::rc::Rc;\n   206→/// use std::cell::RefCell;\n   207→/// use std::collections::VecDeque;\n   208→///\n   209→///\n   210→/// thread_local! {\n   211→///     // A queue containing all tasks ready to do progress\n   212→///     static RUN_QUEUE: RefCell<VecDeque<Rc<Task>>> = RefCell::default();\n   213→/// }\n   214→///\n   215→/// type BoxedFuture = Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = ()>>>;\n   216→///\n   217→/// struct Task(RefCell<BoxedFuture>);\n   218→///\n   219→/// impl LocalWake for Task {\n   220→///     fn wake(self: Rc<Self>) {\n   221→///         RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n   222→///             queue.push_back(self)\n   223→///         })\n   224→///     }\n   225→/// }\n   226→///\n   227→/// fn spawn<F>(future: F)\n   228→/// where\n   229→///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Send + Sync\n   230→/// {\n   231→///     let task = RefCell::new(Box::pin(future));\n   232→///     RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n   233→///         queue.push_back(Rc::new(Task(task)));\n   234→///     });\n   235→/// }\n   236→///\n   237→/// fn block_on<F>(future: F)\n   238→/// where\n   239→///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Sync + Send\n   240→/// {\n   241→///     spawn(future);\n   242→///     loop {\n   243→///         let Some(task) = RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| queue.pop_front()) else {\n   244→///             // we exit, since there are no more tasks remaining on the queue\n   245→///             return;\n   246→///         };\n   247→///\n   248→///         // cast the Rc<Task> into a `LocalWaker`\n   249→///         let local_waker: LocalWaker = task.clone().into();\n   250→///         // Build the context using `ContextBuilder`\n   251→///         let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\n   252→///             .local_waker(&local_waker)\n   253→///             .build();\n   254→///\n   255→///         // Poll the task\n   256→///         let _ = task.0\n   257→///             .borrow_mut()\n   258→///             .as_mut()\n   259→///             .poll(&mut cx);\n   260→///     }\n   261→/// }\n   262→///\n   263→/// block_on(async {\n   264→///     println!(\"hello world\");\n   265→/// });\n   266→/// ```\n   267→///\n   268→#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   269→pub trait LocalWake {\n   270→    /// Wake this task.\n   271→    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n   272→    fn wake(self: Rc<Self>);\n   273→\n   274→    /// Wake this task without consuming the local waker.\n   275→    ///\n   276→    /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\n   277→    /// waker, it should override this method. Types and Traits for working with asynchronous tasks.\n//!\n//! **Note**: Some of the types in this module are only available\n//! on platforms that support atomic loads and stores of pointers.\n//! This may be detected at compile time using\n//! `#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]`.\n\nuse core::mem::ManuallyDrop;\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\nuse core::task::Waker;\nuse core::task::{LocalWaker, RawWaker, RawWakerVTable};\n\nuse crate::rc::Rc;\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\nuse crate::sync::Arc;\n\n/// The implementation of waking a task on an executor.\n///\n/// This trait can be used to create a [`Waker`]. An executor can define an\n/// implementation of this trait, and use that to construct a [`Waker`] to pass\n/// to the tasks that are executed on that executor.\n///\n/// This trait is a memory-safe and ergonomic alternative to constructing a\n/// [`RawWaker`]. It supports the common executor design in which the data used\n/// to wake up a task is stored in an [`Arc`]. Some executors (especially\n/// those for embedded systems) cannot use this API, which is why [`RawWaker`]\n/// exists as an alternative for those systems.\n///\n/// To construct a [`Waker`] from some type `W` implementing this trait,\n/// wrap it in an [`Arc<W>`](Arc) and call `Waker::from()` on that.\n/// It is also possible to convert to [`RawWaker`] in the same way.\n///\n/// <!-- Ideally we'd link to the `From` impl, but rustdoc doesn't generate any page for it within\n///      `alloc` because `alloc` neither defines nor re-exports `From` or `Waker`, and we can't\n///      link ../../std/task/struct.Waker.html#impl-From%3CArc%3CW,+Global%3E%3E-for-Waker\n///      without getting a link-checking error in CI. -->\n///\n/// # Examples\n///\n/// A basic `block_on` function that takes a future and runs it to completion on\n/// the current thread.\n///\n/// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. In order to prevent\n/// deadlocks, production-grade implementations will also need to handle\n/// intermediate calls to `thread::unpark` as well as nested invocations.\n///\n/// ```rust\n/// use std::future::Future;\n/// use std::sync::Arc;\n/// use std::task::{Context, Poll, Wake};\n/// use std::thread::{self, Thread};\n/// use core::pin::pin;\n///\n/// /// A waker that wakes up the current thread when called.\n/// struct ThreadWaker(Thread);\n///\n/// impl Wake for ThreadWaker {\n///     fn wake(self: Arc<Self>) {\n///         self.0.unpark();\n///     }\n/// }\n///\n/// /// Run a future to completion on the current thread.\n/// fn block_on<T>(fut: impl Future<Output = T>) -> T {\n///     // Pin the future so it can be polled.\n///     let mut fut = pin!(fut);\n///\n///     // Create a new context to be passed to the future.\n///     let t = thread::current();\n///     let waker = Arc::new(ThreadWaker(t)).into();\n///     let mut cx = Context::from_waker(&waker);\n///\n///     // Run the future to completion.\n///     loop {\n///         match fut.as_mut().poll(&mut cx) {\n///             Poll::Ready(res) => return res,\n///             Poll::Pending => thread::park(),\n///         }\n///     }\n/// }\n///\n/// block_on(async {\n///     println!(\"Hi from inside a future!\");\n/// });\n/// ```\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\npub trait Wake {\n    /// Wake this task.\n    #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n    fn wake(self: Arc<Self>);\n\n    /// Wake this task without consuming the waker.\n    ///\n    /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\n    /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\n    /// [`Arc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\n    ///\n    /// [`wake`]: Wake::wake\n    #[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\n    fn wake_by_ref(self: &Arc<Self>) {\n        self.clone().wake();\n    }\n}\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\nimpl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for Waker {\n    /// Use a [`Wake`]-able type as a `Waker`.\n    ///\n    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n    fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> Waker {\n        // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\n        // a RawWaker from Arc<W>.\n        unsafe { Waker::from_raw(raw_waker(waker)) }\n    }\n}\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n#[stable(feature = \"wake_trait\", since = \"1.51.0\")]\nimpl<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static> From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker {\n    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\n    ///\n    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n    fn from(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n        raw_waker(waker)\n    }\n}\n\n// NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\n// inlining this into the `From<Arc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\n// the safety of `From<Arc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\n// trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\n// explicitly.\n#[cfg(target_has_atomic = \"ptr\")]\n#[inline(always)]\nfn raw_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: Arc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n    // Increment the reference count of the arc to clone it.\n    //\n    // The #[inline(always)] is to ensure that raw_waker and clone_waker are\n    // always generated in the same code generation unit as one another, and\n    // therefore that the structurally identical const-promoted RawWakerVTable\n    // within both functions is deduplicated at LLVM IR code generation time.\n    // This allows optimizing Waker::will_wake to a single pointer comparison of\n    // the vtable pointers, rather than comparing all four function pointers\n    // within the vtables.\n    #[inline(always)]\n    unsafe fn clone_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\n        unsafe { Arc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n        RawWaker::new(\n            waker,\n            &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n        )\n    }\n\n    // Wake by value, moving the Arc into the Wake::wake function\n    unsafe fn wake<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        let waker = unsafe { Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\n        <W as Wake>::wake(waker);\n    }\n\n    // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\n    unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Arc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\n        <W as Wake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\n    }\n\n    // Decrement the reference count of the Arc on drop\n    unsafe fn drop_waker<W: Wake + Send + Sync + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        unsafe { Arc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n    }\n\n    RawWaker::new(\n        Arc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\n        &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n    )\n}\n\n/// An analogous trait to `Wake` but used to construct a `LocalWaker`.\n///\n/// This API works in exactly the same way as `Wake`,\n/// except that it uses an `Rc` instead of an `Arc`,\n/// and the result is a `LocalWaker` instead of a `Waker`.\n///\n/// The benefits of using `LocalWaker` over `Waker` are that it allows the local waker\n/// to hold data that does not implement `Send` and `Sync`. Additionally, it saves calls\n/// to `Arc::clone`, which requires atomic synchronization.\n///\n///\n/// # Examples\n///\n/// This is a simplified example of a `spawn` and a `block_on` function. The `spawn` function\n/// is used to push new tasks onto the run queue, while the block on function will remove them\n/// and poll them. When a task is woken, it will put itself back on the run queue to be polled\n/// by the executor.\n///\n/// **Note:** This example trades correctness for simplicity. A real world example would interleave\n/// poll calls with calls to an io reactor to wait for events instead of spinning on a loop.\n///\n/// ```rust\n/// #![feature(local_waker)]\n/// use std::task::{LocalWake, ContextBuilder, LocalWaker, Waker};\n/// use std::future::Future;\n/// use std::pin::Pin;\n/// use std::rc::Rc;\n/// use std::cell::RefCell;\n/// use std::collections::VecDeque;\n///\n///\n/// thread_local! {\n///     // A queue containing all tasks ready to do progress\n///     static RUN_QUEUE: RefCell<VecDeque<Rc<Task>>> = RefCell::default();\n/// }\n///\n/// type BoxedFuture = Pin<Box<dyn Future<Output = ()>>>;\n///\n/// struct Task(RefCell<BoxedFuture>);\n///\n/// impl LocalWake for Task {\n///     fn wake(self: Rc<Self>) {\n///         RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n///             queue.push_back(self)\n///         })\n///     }\n/// }\n///\n/// fn spawn<F>(future: F)\n/// where\n///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Send + Sync\n/// {\n///     let task = RefCell::new(Box::pin(future));\n///     RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| {\n///         queue.push_back(Rc::new(Task(task)));\n///     });\n/// }\n///\n/// fn block_on<F>(future: F)\n/// where\n///     F: Future<Output=()> + 'static + Sync + Send\n/// {\n///     spawn(future);\n///     loop {\n///         let Some(task) = RUN_QUEUE.with_borrow_mut(|queue| queue.pop_front()) else {\n///             // we exit, since there are no more tasks remaining on the queue\n///             return;\n///         };\n///\n///         // cast the Rc<Task> into a `LocalWaker`\n///         let local_waker: LocalWaker = task.clone().into();\n///         // Build the context using `ContextBuilder`\n///         let mut cx = ContextBuilder::from_waker(Waker::noop())\n///             .local_waker(&local_waker)\n///             .build();\n///\n///         // Poll the task\n///         let _ = task.0\n///             .borrow_mut()\n///             .as_mut()\n///             .poll(&mut cx);\n///     }\n/// }\n///\n/// block_on(async {\n///     println!(\"hello world\");\n/// });\n/// ```\n///\n#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\npub trait LocalWake {\n    /// Wake this task.\n    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n    fn wake(self: Rc<Self>);\n\n    /// Wake this task without consuming the local waker.\n    ///\n    /// If an executor supports a cheaper way to wake without consuming the\n    /// waker, it should override this method. By default, it clones the\n    /// [`Rc`] and calls [`wake`] on the clone.\n    ///\n    /// [`wake`]: LocalWaker::wake\n    #[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\n    fn wake_by_ref(self: &Rc<Self>) {\n        self.clone().wake();\n    }\n}\n\n#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\nimpl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for LocalWaker {\n    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `LocalWaker`.\n    ///\n    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n    fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> LocalWaker {\n        // SAFETY: This is safe because raw_waker safely constructs\n        // a RawWaker from Rc<W>.\n        unsafe { LocalWaker::from_raw(local_raw_waker(waker)) }\n    }\n}\n#[allow(ineffective_unstable_trait_impl)]\n#[unstable(feature = \"local_waker\", issue = \"118959\")]\nimpl<W: LocalWake + 'static> From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker {\n    /// Use a `Wake`-able type as a `RawWaker`.\n    ///\n    /// No heap allocations or atomic operations are used for this conversion.\n    fn from(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n        local_raw_waker(waker)\n    }\n}\n\n// NB: This private function for constructing a RawWaker is used, rather than\n// inlining this into the `From<Rc<W>> for RawWaker` impl, to ensure that\n// the safety of `From<Rc<W>> for Waker` does not depend on the correct\n// trait dispatch - instead both impls call this function directly and\n// explicitly.\n#[inline(always)]\nfn local_raw_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: Rc<W>) -> RawWaker {\n    // Increment the reference count of the Rc to clone it.\n    //\n    // Refer to the comment on raw_waker's clone_waker regarding why this is\n    // always inline.\n    #[inline(always)]\n    unsafe fn clone_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) -> RawWaker {\n        unsafe { Rc::increment_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n        RawWaker::new(\n            waker,\n            &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n        )\n    }\n\n    // Wake by value, moving the Rc into the LocalWake::wake function\n    unsafe fn wake<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        let waker = unsafe { Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W) };\n        <W as LocalWake>::wake(waker);\n    }\n\n    // Wake by reference, wrap the waker in ManuallyDrop to avoid dropping it\n    unsafe fn wake_by_ref<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        let waker = unsafe { ManuallyDrop::new(Rc::from_raw(waker as *const W)) };\n        <W as LocalWake>::wake_by_ref(&waker);\n    }\n\n    // Decrement the reference count of the Rc on drop\n    unsafe fn drop_waker<W: LocalWake + 'static>(waker: *const ()) {\n        unsafe { Rc::decrement_strong_count(waker as *const W) };\n    }\n\n    RawWaker::new(\n        Rc::into_raw(waker) as *const (),\n        &RawWakerVTable::new(clone_waker::<W>, wake::<W>, wake_by_ref::<W>, drop_waker::<W>),\n    )\n}\n","numLines":351,"startLine":1,"totalLines":351}}}

standard library. The core waker mechanism is found in `library/core/src/task/wake.rs`, which contains the `RawWaker` struct (a data pointer paired with a static vtable) and `RawWakerVTable` struct (which contains function pointers for cloning, waking, waking-by-ref, and dropping). The `Waker` struct wraps a `RawWaker` and is thread-safe (Send+Sync), while `LocalWaker` is a non-thread-safe variant. The `Context` struct holds a reference to a `Waker` (and optionally a `LocalWaker`) and is passed to future polling.\\n\\nThe polling mechanism is split between several files: `library/core/src/task/poll.rs` defines the `Poll` enum (Ready/Pending), and `library/core/src/future/future.rs` defines the `Future` trait with the core `poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output>` method. The future polling loop is executed by runtime executors that repeatedly call `Future::poll()` with a `Context` containing a `Waker` - this is exemplified in the documentation examples in `library/alloc/src/task.rs` in the `block_on` function.\\n\\nA safe interface for creating wakers is provided in `library/alloc/src/task.rs` through the `Wake` trait (for thread-safe Arc-based wakers) and `LocalWake` trait (for Rc-based thread-local wakers). These traits use helper functions `raw_waker()` and `local_raw_waker()` to construct `RawWaker` instances with appropriate vtables that manage reference counting and delegate wake calls to the trait implementations.\\n\\nThe helper macro `ready!` in `library/core/src/task/ready.rs` provides syntactic sugar for handling Poll::Pending in polling code, allowing early returns from polling functions.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":141,"cache_read_input_tokens":57480,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":141},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"eb3b0453-2e98-4d19-a020-7f04f13ed247","uuid":"8768614f-1132-4147-a105-95cb6e55faf7"}

The `Waker` struct wraps a `RawWaker` and is thread-safe (Send+Sync), while `LocalWaker` is a non-thread-safe variant. The `Context` struct holds a reference to a `Waker` (and optionally a `LocalWaker`) and is passed to future polling.\\n\\nThe polling mechanism is split between several files: `library/core/src/task/poll.rs` defines the `Poll` enum (Ready/Pending), and `library/core/src/future/future.rs` defines the `Future` trait with the core `poll(self: Pin<&mut Self>, cx: &mut Context<'_>) -> Poll<Self::Output>` method. The future polling loop is executed by runtime executors that repeatedly call `Future::poll()` with a `Context` containing a `Waker` - this is exemplified in the documentation examples in `library/alloc/src/task.rs` in the `block_on` function.\\n\\nA safe interface for creating wakers is provided in `library/alloc/src/task.rs` through the `Wake` trait (for thread-safe Arc-based wakers) and `LocalWake` trait (for Rc-based thread-local wakers). These traits use helper functions `raw_waker()` and `local_raw_waker()` to construct `RawWaker` instances with appropriate vtables that manage reference counting and delegate wake calls to the trait implementations.\\n\\nThe helper macro `ready!` in `library/core/src/task/ready.rs` provides syntactic sugar for handling Poll::Pending in polling code, allowing early returns from polling functions.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
